500</a>\n</td>\n<td>1979\n</td>\n<td>1983\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10" title="McDonnell Douglas DC-10">McDonnell Douglas DC-10</a>\n</td>\n<td>1988\n</td>\n<td>1999\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vickers_VC10" title="Vickers VC10">Vickers VC10</a>\n</td>\n<td>1974\n</td>\n<td>1981\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vickers_Vanguard" title="Vickers Vanguard">Vickers Vanguard</a>\n</td>\n<td>1974\n</td>\n<td>1975\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a>\n</td>\n<td>1974\n</td>\n<td>1982\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Airways_Engineering">British Airways Engineering</span></h3>\n<p>The company has its own <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Engineering" title="British Airways Engineering">engineering branch</a> to maintain its aircraft fleet, this includes line maintenance at over 70 airports around the world.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> As well as hangar facilities at Heathrow and Gatwick airport it has two major maintenance centres at <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Airport" title="Glasgow Airport">Glasgow</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Maintenance_Cardiff" title="British Airways Maintenance Cardiff">Cardiff Airports</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Branding">Branding</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:British_Airways_at_Terminal_5_in_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/British_Airways_at_Terminal_5_in_2011.jpg/220px-British_Airways_at_Terminal_5_in_2011.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/British_Airways_at_Terminal_5_in_2011.jpg/330px-British_Airways_at_Terminal_5_in_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/British_Airways_at_Terminal_5_in_2011.jpg/440px-British_Airways_at_Terminal_5_in_2011.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:British_Airways_at_Terminal_5_in_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British Airways\' promotional banner above the check in desks at <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Terminal_5" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow Terminal 5">Terminal 5</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Typeface_sample_Mylius_Modern.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Typeface_sample_Mylius_Modern.png/220px-Typeface_sample_Mylius_Modern.png" width="220" height="286" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Typeface_sample_Mylius_Modern.png/330px-Typeface_sample_Mylius_Modern.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Typeface_sample_Mylius_Modern.png/440px-Typeface_sample_Mylius_Modern.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="1040" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Typeface_sample_Mylius_Modern.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mylius Modern, a custom-made typeface used by British Airways</div></div></div>\n<p>The musical theme predominantly used on British Airways advertising is <i>"<a href="/wiki/The_Flower_Duet" class="mw-redirect" title="The Flower Duet">The Flower Duet</a>"</i> by <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9o_Delibes" title="L\xc3\xa9o Delibes">L\xc3\xa9o Delibes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> This, and the slogan "The World\'s Favourite Airline" were introduced in 1989 with the launch of the iconic <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_face_advertisement" title="British Airways face advertisement">"Face" advertisement</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> The slogan was dropped in 2001 after Lufthansa overtook BA in terms of passenger numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> "Flower Duet" is still used by the airline, and has been through several different arrangements since 1989. The most recent version of this melody was shown in 2007 with a new slogan: "Upgrade to British Airways".<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> Other advertising slogans have included "The World\'s Best Airline", "We\'ll Take More Care of You", and "Fly the Flag".<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BA had an account for 23 years with <a href="/wiki/Saatchi_%26_Saatchi" title="Saatchi &amp; Saatchi">Saatchi &amp; Saatchi</a>, an agency that created many of their most famous advertisements, including the influential "Face" campaign. Saatchi &amp; Saatchi later imitated this advert for <a href="/wiki/Silverjet" title="Silverjet">Silverjet</a>, a rival of BA, after BA discontinued their business activities.<sup id="cite_ref-SJA_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SJA-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> Since 2007, BA has used <a href="/wiki/Bartle_Bogle_Hegarty" title="Bartle Bogle Hegarty">Bartle Bogle Hegarty</a> as its advertising agency.<sup id="cite_ref-adref_155-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adref-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>British Airways purchased the <a href="/wiki/Internet_domain" class="mw-redirect" title="Internet domain">internet domain</a> ba.com in 2002 from previous owner <a href="/wiki/Bell_Atlantic" class="mw-redirect" title="Bell Atlantic">Bell Atlantic</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> \'BA\' being the company\'s acronym and its <a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association" title="International Air Transport Association">IATA</a> Airline code. In 2011, BA launched its biggest advertising campaign in a decade, including a 90-second cinematic advert celebrating the airline\'s ninety-year heritage and a new slogan "To Fly. To Serve".<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>British Airways is the official airline of the <a href="/wiki/The_Championships,_Wimbledon" title="The Championships, Wimbledon">Wimbledon Championship tennis tournament</a>, and was the official airline and tier one partner of the <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Olympics" title="2012 Summer Olympics">2012 Summer Olympics</a> and <a href="/wiki/2012_Summer_Paralympics" title="2012 Summer Paralympics">Paralympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> British Airways was also the official airline of England\'s bid to host the <a href="/wiki/2018_and_2022_FIFA_World_Cup_bids" title="2018 and 2022 FIFA World Cup bids">2018 Football World Cup</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><i>High Life</i>, founded in 1973, is the official in-flight magazine of the airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Liveries_and_tail_fins">Liveries and tail fins</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_ethnic_liveries" title="British Airways ethnic liveries">British Airways ethnic liveries</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Animalstrees.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Animalstrees.jpg/220px-Animalstrees.jpg" width="220" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/73/Animalstrees.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="280" data-file-height="246" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Animalstrees.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A British Airways Boeing 747-400 with a Utopia fin</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:British_Airways,_Boeing_777-200ER,_G-YMMH_-_LHR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/British_Airways%2C_Boeing_777-200ER%2C_G-YMMH_-_LHR.jpg/220px-British_Airways%2C_Boeing_777-200ER%2C_G-YMMH_-_LHR.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/British_Airways%2C_Boeing_777-200ER%2C_G-YMMH_-_LHR.jpg/330px-British_Airways%2C_Boeing_777-200ER%2C_G-YMMH_-_LHR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/British_Airways%2C_Boeing_777-200ER%2C_G-YMMH_-_LHR.jpg/440px-British_Airways%2C_Boeing_777-200ER%2C_G-YMMH_-_LHR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3020" data-file-height="2016" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:British_Airways,_Boeing_777-200ER,_G-YMMH_-_LHR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A BA Boeing 777-200 with a Panda face, marking the launch of a route from London to <a href="/wiki/Chengdu" title="Chengdu">Chengdu</a> in 2013</div></div></div>\n<p>Since its formation in 1974, British Airways\' aeroplanes carried a <a href="/wiki/Union_Jack" title="Union Jack">Union Jack</a> scheme painted on their tail fins. The original tail scheme was changed in 1984 as part of a new livery designed by <a href="/wiki/Landor_Associates" title="Landor Associates">Landor Associates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1997, there was a controversial change from the use of the former British Airways branding (which incorporated stylised elements of the <a href="/wiki/Union_Jack" title="Union Jack">Union Jack</a>) to a new livery which was intended mainly to reflect the diversity of places served by the airline \xe2\x80\x93 so-called "World Images". This involved a range of different designs appearing on tailfins and elsewhere, although the bodies of all the planes would use the corporate colours consistently; the exception was the Concorde fleet, which would have a new tailfin design based on a stylised, fluttering Union flag.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> What became known as the "ethnic images" included Delftware or Chinese calligraphy, related to countries on the company\'s network of routes. This was reported to have caused problems with <a href="/wiki/Air_traffic_control" title="Air traffic control">air traffic control</a>: previously controllers had been able to tell pilots to follow a BA plane, but they were now harder to visually identify.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Several people spoke out against the change, including the former Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Thatcher" title="Margaret Thatcher">Margaret Thatcher</a>, who famously covered the tail of a model 747 at an event with a handkerchief, to show her displeasure.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> BA\'s traditional rival, Virgin Atlantic, took advantage of the negative press coverage by applying the Union flag to the winglets of their aircraft along with the slogan "Britain\'s national flagcarrier".<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> In 1999, the CEO of British Airways, Bob Ayling, announced that all BA planes would adopt the tailfin design originally intended to be used only on the Concorde, based on the Union Flag.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Loyalty_programmes">Loyalty programmes</span></h3>\n<p>British Airways\' tiered loyalty programme, called the Executive Club, includes access to special lounges and dedicated "fast" queues.<sup id="cite_ref-execclub_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-execclub-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> BA also invites its top corporate accounts to join a "Premier" incentive programme. British Airways operates airside lounges for passengers travelling in premium cabins, and these are available to certain tiers of Executive Club members.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> First class passengers, as well as Gold Executive Club members, are entitled to use First Class Lounges. Business class passengers (called Club World or Club Europe in BA terms) as well as Silver Executive Club members may use Business lounges.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> At airports in which BA does not operate a departure lounge, a third party lounge is often provided for premium or status passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> In 2011, due to the merger with Iberia, British Airways announced changes to the Executive Club to maximise integration between the airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> This included the combination and rebranding of <a href="/wiki/Air_Miles#Air_Miles_United_Kingdom" title="Air Miles">Air Miles</a>, BA Miles and Iberia Plus points as the IAG operated loyalty programme <a href="/wiki/Avios" class="mw-redirect" title="Avios">Avios</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inflight_magazines">Inflight magazines</span></h3>\n<p><i><b>high life Magazine</b></i> is British Airways\' complimentary inflight magazine. It is available to all customers across all cabins and aircraft types.\n</p><p><i><b>high life shop Magazine</b></i> is British Airways\' inflight shopping magazine. It is available to all customers on all aircraft where the inflight shopping range can be carried.\n</p><p><i><b>First life</b></i> is a complimentary magazine offered to all customers travelling in the First cabin. It has a range of articles including fashion, trends and technology with an upmarket target audience.\n</p><p><i><b>Business life</b></i> is a complimentary magazine targeted at business travellers and frequent flyers. The magazine can be found in all short haul aircraft seat pockets, in the magazine selection for Club World customers and in lounges operated by British Airways.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cabins_and_services">Cabins and services</span></h2>\n<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303569"/><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:British_Airways_A321_Y_cabin,_GB_(GT)_March_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/British_Airways_A321_Y_cabin%2C_GB_%28GT%29_March_2008.jpg/220px-British_Airways_A321_Y_cabin%2C_GB_%28GT%29_March_2008.jpg" width="220" height="165" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/British_Airways_A321_Y_cabin%2C_GB_%28GT%29_March_2008.jpg/330px-British_Airways_A321_Y_cabin%2C_GB_%28GT%29_March_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/British_Airways_A321_Y_cabin%2C_GB_%28GT%29_March_2008.jpg/440px-British_Airways_A321_Y_cabin%2C_GB_%28GT%29_March_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">A short haul <a href="/wiki/Economy_class" title="Economy class">Euro Traveller</a> cabin</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:BA_New_Club_World_seat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/BA_New_Club_World_seat.jpg/220px-BA_New_Club_World_seat.jpg" width="220" height="188" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/BA_New_Club_World_seat.jpg/330px-BA_New_Club_World_seat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/BA_New_Club_World_seat.jpg/440px-BA_New_Club_World_seat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="831" data-file-height="711" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">A Next-Generation <a href="/wiki/Business_class" title="Business class">Club World</a> seat in long-haul</div></div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Short_haul">Short haul</span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_class">Economy class</span></h4>\n<p><i>Euro Traveller</i> is British Airways\' economy class cabin on all short-haul flights within Europe, including domestic flights within the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-ST_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ST-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\nHeathrow based flights are operated by Airbus A320 series aircraft and Boeing 767-300ER aircraft. Gatwick based flights are operated by Airbus A320 series aircraft. Standard seat pitch varies from 29" to 34" depending on aircraft type and location of seat.\n</p><p>All flights from Heathrow and Gatwick have a <a href="/wiki/Buy_on_board" title="Buy on board">buy on board</a> system with a range of food provided by <a href="/wiki/Marks_and_Spencer" class="mw-redirect" title="Marks and Spencer">Marks and Spencer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> \nPurchases can only be made by using credit and debit card or by using Frequent Flyer Avios points.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Scheduled services operated by <a href="/wiki/BA_CityFlyer" title="BA CityFlyer">BA CityFlyer</a> currently offer complimentary onboard catering. The service will switch to buy on board in the near future.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_class">Business class</span></h4>\n<p><i>Club Europe</i> is the short-haul business class on all short-haul flights. This class allows for access to business lounges at most airports.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> Club Europe provides seats in a 2\xe2\x80\x932 configuration on narrowbody aircraft, with the middle seat not used. Instead, a table folds up from under the middle seat on refurbished aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-BAP_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BAP-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Pillows and blankets are available on longer flights.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/In-flight_entertainment" title="In-flight entertainment">In-flight entertainment</a> is offered on selected longer flights operated by the Boeing 767-300ER and some A320 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Complimentary headphones are provided to all customers on services where IFE is available.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mid-haul_and_Long_haul">Mid-haul and Long haul</span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="First_class">First class</span></h4>\n<p><i>First</i> is offered on British Airways\' Airbus A380s, Boeing 747-400s, Boeing 777-300ERs, Boeing 787-9s and on some of their Boeing 777-200s. There are fourteen (eight on 787-9) private cabins on most of these aircraft, each with a 6&#160;ft 6&#160;in (1.98&#160;m) bed, a 15-inch (38&#160;cm) wide entertainment screen, and in-seat power.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\nDedicated British Airways \'Galleries First\' lounges are available at some airports. The exclusive \'Concorde Room\' lounges at Heathrow Terminal 5 and New York JFK airports offer pre-flight dining with waiter service and more intimate space. Business lounges are used where these are not available.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Club_World">Club World</span></h4>\n<p><i>Club World</i> is the mid-haul and long-haul <a href="/wiki/Business_class" title="Business class">business class</a> cabin. It is offered on all Boeing 777, Boeing 787, Boeing 747-400, Airbus A318,  Airbus A380, and selected Airbus A321 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CWL_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CWL-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> The cabin features fully convertible flat bed seats. In 2006, British Airways launched <i>Next Generation New Club World</i>, featuring larger seats.<sup id="cite_ref-BAP_16-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BAP-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The Club World cabins are all configured in a similar design on widebody aircraft with aisle seats facing forwards, while middle seats and window seats face backwards (British Airways is one of only five carriers with backwards facing Business class seats; <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">Qatar Airways</a> are the others).\n</p><p>On mid-haul routes operated by Airbus A321s, an alternating 1:2 / 2:1 configuration of 23 seats is used in the front section of the aircraft.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Traveller_Plus">World Traveller Plus</span></h4>\n<p><i>World Traveller Plus</i> is the <a href="/wiki/Premium_economy" title="Premium economy">premium economy</a> class cabin provided on all A380, B747, B777, and B787 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-ST_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ST-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> This cabin offers wider seats, extended leg-room, additional seat comforts such as larger IFE screen (on most aircraft) a foot rest and power sockets.<sup id="cite_ref-WTP_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WTP-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> A complimentary \'World Traveller\' bar is offered along with an upgraded main meal course.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Traveller">World Traveller</span></h4>\n<p><i>World Traveller</i> is the mid-haul and long-haul economy class cabin. It offers seat-back entertainment, complimentary food and drink, pillows, and blankets.<sup id="cite_ref-ST_173-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ST-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WTNC_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WTNC-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> AVOD personal TV screens are available on all A321s, A380s, B747s, B777s, and B787s.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup> AC power outlets and USB plug-in points are offered in every seat row on the Airbus A380, Boeing 787, Boeing 777-300ER and on refurbished 777-200 aircraft. The outlets accept both UK and US plugs.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents_and_accidents">Incidents and accidents</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BA38_Crash.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/BA38_Crash.jpg/220px-BA38_Crash.jpg" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/BA38_Crash.jpg/330px-BA38_Crash.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/BA38_Crash.jpg/440px-BA38_Crash.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2896" data-file-height="1944" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BA38_Crash.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The damaged British Airways Flight 38 on 17 January 2008</div></div></div>\n<ul><li>On 22 November 1974, British Airways Flight 870 was hijacked shortly after take-off from <a href="/wiki/Dubai" title="Dubai">Dubai</a> for London Heathrow. The <a href="/wiki/Vickers_VC10" title="Vickers VC10">Vickers VC10</a> landed at <a href="/wiki/Tripoli" title="Tripoli">Tripoli</a> for refuelling before flying on to Tunis. The captain, Jim Futcher, returned to the aircraft to fly it knowing the hijackers were on board. The hijackers eventually surrendered after 84 hours, but not before a hostage was murdered. Futcher was awarded the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Gallantry_Medal" title="Queen&#39;s Gallantry Medal">Queen\'s Gallantry Medal</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Guild_of_Air_Pilots_and_Air_Navigators" class="mw-redirect" title="Guild of Air Pilots and Air Navigators">Guild of Air Pilots and Air Navigators</a> Founders Medal, the <a href="/wiki/British_Air_Line_Pilots_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="British Air Line Pilots Association">British Air Line Pilots Association</a> Gold Medal and a Certificate of Commendation from British Airways for his actions during the hijacking.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Medals_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Medals-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 10 September 1976, a <a href="/wiki/Hawker_Siddeley_Trident" title="Hawker Siddeley Trident">Trident 3B</a> on <a href="/wiki/1976_Zagreb_mid-air_collision" title="1976 Zagreb mid-air collision">British Airways Flight 476</a> departed from London Heathrow to Istanbul. It collided in mid-air with an <a href="/wiki/Inex_Adria" class="mw-redirect" title="Inex Adria">Inex Adria</a> <a href="/wiki/McDonnell-Douglas_DC-9" class="mw-redirect" title="McDonnell-Douglas DC-9">DC9-31</a> near <a href="/wiki/Zagreb" title="Zagreb">Zagreb</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> All 54 passengers and 9 crew members on the BA aircraft died. This is the only fatal accident to a British Airways aircraft since the company\'s formation in 1974.</li>\n<li>On 24 June 1982, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Flight_9" title="British Airways Flight 9">British Airways Flight 9</a>, a Boeing 747-200 registration <i>G-BDXH</i>, flew through a cloud of volcanic ash and dust from the eruption of <a href="/wiki/Galunggung" title="Galunggung">Mount Galunggung</a>. The ash and dust caused extensive damage to the aircraft, including the failure of all four engines.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> The crew managed to glide the plane out of the dust cloud and restart all four of its engines, although one later had to be shut down again. The volcanic ash caused the cockpit window to be scratched to such an extent that it was difficult for the pilots to see out of the plane. However, the aircraft made a successful emergency landing at <a href="/wiki/Halim_Perdanakusuma_International_Airport" title="Halim Perdanakusuma International Airport">Halim Perdanakusuma International Airport</a> just outside <a href="/wiki/Jakarta" title="Jakarta">Jakarta</a>. There were no fatalities or injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-Black_Box_192-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Black_Box-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 22 August 1985, <a href="/wiki/British_Airtours_Flight_28M" title="British Airtours Flight 28M">British Airtours Flight 28M</a> caught fire after an aborted take off at <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a> while on a charter flight to the <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greek</a> island of <a href="/wiki/Corfu" title="Corfu">Corfu</a>. The fuel access panel on the aircraft\'s fuselage was pierced by a part of the <a href="/wiki/Gas_compressor" class="mw-redirect" title="Gas compressor">compressor</a> that had been ejected from the port engine as a result of a malfunction. The fire quickly engulfed the area around the rear of the plane filling the cabin with toxic fumes. Fifty-three passengers and two crew members died as a result - most of them dying of <a href="/wiki/Asphyxiation" class="mw-redirect" title="Asphyxiation">asphyxiation</a> after inhaling the fumes.</li>\n<li>On 10 June 1990, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Flight_5390" title="British Airways Flight 5390">British Airways Flight 5390</a>, a <a href="/wiki/BAC_One-Eleven" title="BAC One-Eleven">BAC One-Eleven</a> flight between <a href="/wiki/Birmingham" title="Birmingham">Birmingham</a> and <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1laga" title="M\xc3\xa1laga">M\xc3\xa1laga</a>, suffered a windscreen blowout due to the fitting of incorrect bolts the previous day. The Captain suffered major injuries after being partially blown out of the aircraft, but the co-pilot landed the plane safely at <a href="/wiki/Southampton_Airport" title="Southampton Airport">Southampton Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-OgdenInterview_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OgdenInterview-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 2 August 1990, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Flight_149" title="British Airways Flight 149">British Airways Flight 149</a> landed at <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_International_Airport" title="Kuwait International Airport">Kuwait International Airport</a> four hours after the Iraqi invasion of <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>. The aircraft, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747-100</a> <i>G-AWND</i>, was destroyed, and all passengers and crew were captured. Two of the landing gears were salvaged, and are on display in Waterside, BA Headquarters in London.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 29 December 2000, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Flight_2069" title="British Airways Flight 2069">British Airways Flight 2069</a> was en route from London to Nairobi when a mentally-ill passenger entered the cockpit and grabbed the controls. As the pilots struggled to remove the intruder, the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a> stalled twice and banked to 94 degrees. Several people on board were injured by the violent manoeuvres, which briefly caused the aircraft to descend at 30,000&#160;ft per minute. The man was finally restrained with the help of several passengers, and the co-pilot regained control of the aircraft. The flight landed safely in Nairobi.</li>\n<li>On 17 January 2008, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Flight_38" title="British Airways Flight 38">British Airways Flight 38</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">Boeing 777-200ER</a> <i>G-YMMM</i>, from <a href="/wiki/Beijing_Capital_International_Airport" title="Beijing Capital International Airport">Beijing</a> to London crash-landed approximately 1,000 feet (300&#160;m) short of London Heathrow Airport\'s runway 27L, and slid onto the runway\'s <a href="/wiki/Displaced_threshold" title="Displaced threshold">displaced threshold</a>. The aircraft sustained damage to its landing gear, wing roots and engines, resulting in the first hull loss of a Boeing 777. There were no fatalities, but there was one serious injury and 12 minor injuries. The accident was caused by icing in the fuel system, resulting in a loss of power.</li>\n<li>On 24 May 2013, <a href="/w/index.php?title=British_Airways_Flight_762&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="British Airways Flight 762 (page does not exist)">British Airways Flight 762</a>, using an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319-131" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A319-131">Airbus A319-131</a> and registered as G-EUOE, returned to <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow Airport</a> after fan cowl doors detached from both engines shortly after take off. During the approach a fire broke out in the right engine and persisted after the engine was shut down. The aircraft landed safely with no injuries to the 80 people on board. A preliminary accident report revealed that the cowlings had been left unlatched following overnight maintenance. The separation of the doors caused airframe damage and the right hand engine fire resulted from a ruptured fuel pipe.</li>\n<li>On 22 December 2013, British Airways Flight 34, a Boeing 747\xe2\x80\x93436 <i>G-BNLL</i>, hit a building at <a href="/wiki/O._R._Tambo_International_Airport" title="O. R. Tambo International Airport">O. R. Tambo International Airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Johannesburg" title="Johannesburg">Johannesburg</a> after missing a turning on a taxiway. The starboard wing was severely damaged but there were no injuries amongst the crew or 189 passengers, however four members of ground staff were injured when the wing smashed into the building.<sup id="cite_ref-Tel10534084_196-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tel10534084-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> The aircraft was officially withdrawn from service in February 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-BASourceBNLL_197-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BASourceBNLL-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 8 September 2015, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_Flight_2276" title="British Airways Flight 2276">British Airways Flight 2276</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 777-200">Boeing 777-236ER</a> <i>G-VIIO</i>, aborted its takeoff at <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas" title="Las Vegas">Las Vegas</a> <a href="/wiki/McCarran_International_Airport" title="McCarran International Airport">McCarran International Airport</a> due to an <a href="/wiki/Uncontained_engine_failure" class="mw-redirect" title="Uncontained engine failure">uncontained engine failure</a> <sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> of its left (<a href="/wiki/Aircraft_engine_position_number" class="mw-redirect" title="Aircraft engine position number">#1</a>) <a href="/wiki/General_Electric_GE90" title="General Electric GE90">General Electric GE90</a> engine, which led to a substantial fire. The aircraft was evacuated on the main runway. All 157 passengers and 13 crew escaped the aircraft, at least 14 people sustaining minor injuries.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span Kingdom</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_the_United_Kingdom_and_the_British_Crown_Dependencies" title="List of airports in the United Kingdom and the British Crown Dependencies">List of airports in the United Kingdom and the British Crown Dependencies</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Transport_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Transport in the United Kingdom">Transport in the United Kingdom</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Plane_Saver_Credit_Union" title="Plane Saver Credit Union">Plane Saver Credit Union</a></li></ul>\n<table role="presentation" class="noprint navbox metadata
